Full preservation l] **The Cyprus Defense Dilemma**

Cyprus faces an impossible choice: maintain strict neutrality while hosting 3,000 British military personnel at RAF Akrotiri, or accept that UK defensive operations make the island a legitimate target in regional conflicts, as demonstrated when Iran fired two missiles toward Cyprus in March 2026.

**Plan A - Enforce Strict Neutrality:** Prime Minister Christodoulides declares Cyprus "not involved in this conflict in any way" and prohibits offensive operations from British bases. Benefits include protecting Cyprus's non-aligned status, reducing Iranian targeting risk, and maintaining diplomatic relationships with all regional actors. Costs include inability to actually control British sovereign base operations, potential damage to UK alliance, and vulnerability to collateral damage while British personnel remain potential targets regardless of declarations.

**Plan B - Accept De Facto Military Role:** Allow British "defensive operations" including intercepting missiles threatening allies like Qatar. Benefits include contributing to regional air defense, protecting British personnel, and maintaining alliance credibility. Costs include violating stated neutrality policy, making Cyprus a legitimate military target, creating legal tensions over sovereign territory use, and losing diplomatic flexibility with regional actors.

Neither plan resolves the structural incompatibility: Cyprus cannot simultaneously be neutral territory and host active military bases conducting regional defense operations.

**What should be done? Justify your position. Identify what you would sacrifice and what you refuse to sacrifice, and why.** result=HOLD approval=5% veto=True

**Plan A (UK Defensive Patrols):** Deploy UK aircraft from Qatar for ongoing defensive intercepts across the region, protecting personnel in Cyprus, Bahrain, and Qatar without offensive actions. **Plan B (Cyprus Strict Neutrality):** Refuse any UK/US offensive use of Cyprus bases, limiting involvement to emergency protocols only. Costs: Exposes 1.2 million Cypriots to stray missiles, potential €500M+ economic hit from tourism collapse. Benefits: Preserves neutrality, avoids entanglement in US-Israel-Iran war. Drawbacks: Strains UK alliance, risks base abandonment, leaves 3,000 personnel exposed without full Cypriot support.

Full preservation l] **Policy Dilemma: Cyprus Military Base Defense Crisis**

On March 1, 2026, Iran launched two ballistic missiles at RAF Akrotiri in Cyprus, housing 3,000 British personnel, following strikes that killed Iran's Supreme Leader. This marks the first direct Iranian attack on UK sovereign bases in Cyprus.

**Plan A (UK Escalation):** Deploy additional RAF jets from Cyprus for regional intercept missions at £500 million cost. Benefits: Protects 3,000 UK personnel in Cyprus and 300 in Bahrain through active defense, maintaining 100% interception success rate so far. Drawbacks: Risks provoking targeted Iranian strikes on bases near 250,000 Cypriots, escalates to full UK-Iran conflict within weeks, strains £50bn defense budget.

**Plan B (Cyprus Neutrality):** Refuse UK base overflights for offensive operations, demand purely defensive posture. Benefits: Shields 1.2 million Cypriots from becoming a war zone, avoids months-long retaliation cycle. Costs: €100 million annual economic hit, affects 15,000 local residents dependent on base economy. Drawbacks: Delays intercepts by 24-48 hours per sortie, exposes 3,000 UK personnel to undefended missile strikes.

Neither plan addresses the core problem: ballistic missiles travel at Mach 5+ giving under 5 minutes warning, overwhelming Cyprus's limited S-300 defenses with 10-20% residual hit risk per wave even with active interception.

Full preservation l] **Policy Dilemma: Cyprus Under Fire**

After Iran fired ballistic missiles at UK Sovereign Base Areas in Cyprus on March 1, 2026—following "Operation Epic Fury" that killed Iran's Supreme Leader—the Cyprus government faces an impossible choice between security and neutrality.

**Plan A: Enhanced Base Defense**
The UK proposes deploying RAF defensive patrols and maintaining full operational readiness at Akrotiri, protecting ~3,000 British personnel. This costs £50-100 million in surge operations but deters further Iranian strikes and secures Britain's key Middle East hub. However, it makes Cyprus bases more visible targets, potentially escalating the conflict and drawing Cyprus directly into a regional war.

**Plan B: Strict Neutrality**
Prime Minister Christodoulides demands no offensive operations from bases and emergency protocols to protect 1.2 million Cypriots. This preserves Cyprus's neutrality and protects the £2.5 billion tourism industry (15% of GDP). However, it risks £200-500 million in economic losses from airspace closures (48 flights canceled daily, 10,000+ passengers stranded), and cannot actually control UK sovereign territory or stop Iranian missiles that ignore borders.

Neither plan addresses the core problem: Cyprus sits unavoidably on the Europe-Middle East corridor with unmovable bases within Iran's 2,000km missile range, creating spillover risks regardless of policy choices.

Full preservation l] **Policy Dilemma: Iranian Missile Attack on UK Cyprus Bases**

Iran launched two missiles toward UK Sovereign Base Areas in Cyprus, including RAF Akrotiri hosting 3,000 British personnel, on March 1, 2026, retaliating for Operation Epic Fury strikes that killed Ayatollah Khamenei. This marks the first direct Iranian targeting of these strategic bases amid broader regional attacks.

**Plan A: UK Strengthen Defensive Posture**
Deploy defensive patrols and enhanced base protections at estimated cost of £50-100 million. Benefits: Protects 3,000 personnel, prevents direct hits through interceptions, limits escalation without offensive action. Drawbacks: Strains resources across multiple fronts, risks drawing Cyprus deeper into conflict, alienates Cyprus's neutral stance.

**Plan B: Cyprus Strict Neutrality**
Cyprus demands no UK posture changes, seeking non-targeting guarantees through diplomacy at cost of €10-20 million in emergency protocols. Benefits: Shields 1.26 million Cypriots from spillover, upholds EU neutral policy, prevents base exploitation for operations. Drawbacks: Weakens UK deterrence, exposes island to repeat overflights, pressures bilateral UK-Cyprus treaty arrangements.

Full preservation l] **Policy Dilemma: UK Response to Iranian Missile Strikes on Cyprus**

Iran fired two ballistic missiles toward UK sovereign bases in Cyprus on February 28-29, 2026, retaliating for strikes that killed Supreme Leader Khamenei. The attack threatens 3,000 UK personnel and 1.2 million Cypriots.

**Plan A - Defensive Posture Only**: Maintain RAF patrols to intercept threats without offensive action or allowing US base use. Benefits: Avoids direct war entry, respects Cyprus neutrality, protects 67 million UK citizens from retaliation. Costs: £500M+ annually, leaves bases vulnerable to future attacks (missiles already landed "few hundred yards" from 300 UK troops in Bahrain), provides no deterrence against Iran's 2,000+ km range capabilities.

**Plan B - Limited Offensive Support**: Allow US/Israel use of RAF Akrotiri for strikes on Iranian launch sites within 7 days. Benefits: Deters future launches, neutralizes Iran's escalating threat across 6+ Gulf states, secures bases long-term. Costs: £2B+ in immediate upgrades, risks 50,000+ Cypriot evacuations, violates Cyprus government neutrality, potentially makes Cyprus a primary target.

Neither plan addresses the core problem: Plan A leaves UK assets defenseless against hypersonic-capable missiles that evade interception, while Plan B risks dragging neutral Cyprus into broader war without guaranteed elimination of Iran's missile capabilities.

**What should be done? Justify your position. Identify what you would sacrifice and what you refuse to sacrifice, and why.** result=HOLD approval=-30% veto=True
